K Chief of Campus Police James 
LaPaglia reviews all reports prior 
to release.
K Only three people on The Tar
tan staff see the reports: the Edi
tor in Chief, the News Editor, and
the staffwriter typing the report.
K All personal names of com
plainants, victims, suspects, and 
fraternity names are omitted from 
the printed report. Ethnic descrip
tions and other personal details
are given only in the context of 
complete descriptions.
K Not every incident that occurs 
on campus appears in the report.

Point Perfect.
With Our Student/Faculty Rate.
The Pittsburgh Hilton and Towers is set on the Point of the three rivers and popu
lar Point State Park is our front yard. Three Rivers Stadium, the Carnegie |
Science Center and shopping are all within walking distance. And if 
you dine with us at Sterlings, we can arrange a limousine to the sym
phony, the opera, the theater, or an event at the arena. For reservations, call your

FORUM
Carnegie Mellon University21 April 1997
iggedaa c/ crd Md0 
&edaTgdMcBdydAc
As the new president plans to 
take office on July 1st, he faces 
the task of getting to know CMU.  
Trying to uncover academic and 
social issues that students grapple 
with can be daunting; we would 
like to give the president-elect an 
update on who we are and what 
we care about.
While Dr. Cohons first official 
appearance made a mark on those 
who were able to interact with 
him, students already felt a dis
tance, a common complaint of students during President 
Mehrabians term.
The reception was held at noon
 convenient for faculty mem
bers on lunch break, but an awk
ward time for students who prob
ably have class. This prohibited 
students from hearing Dr. Cohon 
address the campus for the first 
time.
Holding a reception that was 
more accessible and inviting to 
students would have dispelled a 
common belief that the presidents 
role has little to do with the needs 
of students.
One way to overcome this idea 
is for the president to be a visible 
figure on campus. We hope the 
new president will create oppor
tunities for students to interact 
with him, through outlets similar 
to the lunches that administra
tors such as Dean Stearns and 
Dean Murphy hold periodically.
Carrying on the Presidents Stu
dent Advisory Council is another 
way to meet students  a venue 
that has been neglected in the 
last few months. We also hope
that he will support undergradu
ates by attending campus activi
ties where students are the pri
mary audience, such as studio 
theater performances and inter
mural sporting events.
While CMU has national recog
nition in technology and the arts, 
we hope to see the liberal arts 
programs gain the same reputa
tion.
We would like to see more inter
disciplinary programs and com
munication among colleges. It 
seems as though each college on 
this campus operates on its own 
terms and has little or no contact 
with other departments.
This makes it difficult BHA stu
dents, for example, to accomplish 
something as simple as registra
tion since they must always 
struggle with administrators in 
colleges that do not seem to want 
to work together. It also discour
ages students from getting double 
majors or minors because there is 
little support for such overlaps.
Isolation also plagues gradu
ate and undergraduate student 
interaction. With the recent de
bate in Student Senate over 
whether the Graduate Student 
Association should be its own 
governing body, the gap between 
the two faces greater distance. 
As it stands, the two have little 
opportunity to connect their ex
periences.
We would like to welcome Dr. 
Cohon to CMU. Although there 
are many challenges, we hope he 
finds that the campus commu
nity has much to offer.
8-i ar/tyg M/c addp 
bgUTMTacebcTwd rdyv
Once again, Student Senate re
jected the Graduate Student 
Associations plan to make GSA 
an autonomous body, this time by 
just one vote. Frustrated by Stu
dent Senates repeated decision, 
the GSA has threatened to seek 
administrative intervention to 
support their proposal.
By turning to the administra
tion to settle disagreements 
within Student Senate, GSA will 
set a dangerous precedent, one 
tht impedes upon the very pur
pose of the organizationto learn 
how to govern themselves with
out resorting to the guidance of 
an upper-hand.
Student Senate represents the 
student bodys interests and opin
ions to the administration; it 
serves to give students a voice in 
administrative decisions. By opt
ing to give up that right to formu
late a united front from differ
ences in opinion, Student Senate 
and GSA are sending out the 
wrong message.
By looking to the administra
tion to solve this issue, GSA is 
rolling out the red carpet, invit
ing the administration to step in 
to settle future problems. While 
that right might already exist, 
the administration might feel 
more compelled to use it, if GSA 
gives the impression that inter
vention is welcome. If graduate 
students rely on administrative 
intervention now, officials may 
be able to influence the decisions 
of GSA in the future.
pB -----------------------------
Simona Lo/Tartan Art Staff

GSA members argue that the 
lack of participation of graduate 
students in Senate means that 
their interests are under-represented when Senate makes deci
sions that affect the entire stu
dent body, both undergraduates 
and graduates. Yet, the decision 
to reject GSAs proposal a second 
time lost by only one vote.
GSA cannot blame the system 
because the numbers prove that 
undergraduate Senate represen
tatives are considering the needs 
of graduate students before cast
ing their vote.
Senators have been given the 
responsibility to make decisions 
in the interest of all students. 
They have been entrusted to carry 
out this duty and fulfill these re
sponsibilities even when the deci
sions are difficult.
Senate has established bylaws 
that dictate how to resolve diffi
cult problems. Although the by
laws do not specifically prohibit 
GSA from seeking outside inter
vention, they recognize Student 
Senate as an autonomous organi
zation. By overlooking this por
tion of the bylaws, Student Sen
ate would lose its viability as a 
governing body.
To show respect to a system that 
allows students to think on their 
own and truly act as a body that 
represents the strengths and in
terests of CMU students, Student 
Senate and GSA should resolve its 
conflicts independent of the admin
istration.

The Tartan is the student newspaper of 
Carnegie Mellon University. It is a weekly 
newspaper published by students during the 
fall and spring semesters, at no cost to 
members of the University community. It is printed by Western Pennsylvania Printing, Inc. 
Subscriptions are available for the semester or academicyear. The editorials appearing at 
the beginning of the opinion section are The 
officlalopinion of The Tartan editorial board. 
Columns and political cartoons are the 
opinions of individual creators. The Tartan 
reserves the right to reject or condense any 
column or political cartoon. Letters to the 
Editor are opinions of authors who are usually, 
but not necessarily, members ofthe University 
community. A letter intended for publication 
must be signed and include the writer's 
address ancr phone number for verification. 
Names may be withheld upon request. The Tartan requests that letters be no longer than 
500 words. The Tartan reserves the right to condense or r '

Carnegie Mellon sheds some light on campus security
Theres no reason to be in the dark about campus security. A team of Carnegie Mellon police officers, security guards, and housing and student life staff members work to keep students, faculty, staff and visitors informed and safe on the campus and adjacent areas. These professionals are concerned with the safety and welfare of the campus community and are best able to answer questions about campus security.
Crime rates are based on the numbers and categories of crime, divided by the university's total number of students and 
employees. Figures are per one thousand headcount.

The number of rapes reported to Campus Police does not reflect the incidents of sexual assault on our campus, a crime that is 
historically underreported. The U.S. Department of Education, in a study published in 1997, reported .8 reports of forcible sex 
offenses per ten thousand enrollment in private 4-year institutions. The Carnegie Mellon Sexual Assault Advisory Group continually 
works to educate and protect the campus community. For the past three years, the sexual assault advisors received the following 
number of inquiries:
1994 -1
1995 -3
1996-10
How safe are the neighborhoods surrounding our campus?
In order to better understand the statistics concerning crime, Carnegie Mellon exceeds the federal and state requirements by providing crime statistics and rates not only for crimes reported on campus, but also in the surrounding neighborhoods.

1964, Title IX of tho Educational Amendments ol 1972 and Section 504 of the Rehabilitation Act of 1973 or other federal, state, or local laws or executive orders.
In addition, Carnegie Mollon Unlvorslty does not discriminate in admission, employment or administration of Its programs on tho basis of religion, creed, ancestry, belief, age, veteran status, sexual orientation or in violation of federal, state, or local laws or executive orders. However, in the 
judgment o( tho Carneglo Mellon Human Relations Commission, the Department of Defense policy of, "Don't ask, don't tell, don't pursue," excludes openly gay, lesbian and bisexual students from receiving ROTC scholarships or serving in the military. Nevertheless, all ROTC classes at 
Carnoglo Mollon Unlvorslty aro available to all studonts.

Not valid with any other offer. Please mention coupon when ordering. Expires May 31, 1997
Then consider joining Carnegie Mellons Undergraduate Mock Trial Team.
The Undergraduate Mock Trial Team is open to all CMU undergraduates, not 
just members of the Pre-law Society. CMU will host an invitational intercol
legiate mock trial tournament on November 15, 1997. If interested, contact 
Dr. Joseph Devine atjdOx@andrew.cmu.edu.
NOTE: Prospective mock trial participants might want to consider the follow
ing Fall 1997 course: 66-181, Topics in Law, 6 units, Pass/Fail, WF, 3:30
4:20 pm. This course is essentially a professional writing/public speaking/ 
oral argument course, couched in a legal/courtroom context. Its theoretical 
focus is on the structure and rules of U.S. court procedure, with a heavy 
applied emphasis on trial procedure (e.g., the functions, rules and techniques 
of oral arguments in American courtrooms [e.g., opening and closing state
ments], the functions, rules and techniques of witness examinations [directand cross-examinations]), how and why these rules vary with different case 
types (e.g., criminal vs. civil trials), etc. The course has no prerequisites, and 
is open to any undergraduate.
There will be a non-binding relationship between this course and the intercol
legiate mock trial tournament that Carnegie Mellon will hosts in November 
1997. For example, a hypothetical criminal case will be a primary focus of 
the course, and will also be the case argued at this November tournament. 
However, enrollment in the course will not require participation in the mock 
trial tournament; conversely, participation in the tournament will not require 
enrollment in the course.
Register in the H&SS Academic Advisory Center, Baker Hall 161.
Are you...
...thinking about law school, 
and law as a career, or
...a veteran debater interested in 
similar activity at the college 
level, or
...interested in honing your 
public speaking skills?

Student Government
Elections Part II
9/cd7 Polls open Thursday and Friday, April 24 and 25 
Vote 10 a.m. to 2 p.m both days outside Doherty Hall.
(Rain location: Inside Doherty Hall front entrance)
VtM  Petitions for Student Body President, Student Body Treasurer and 
Senator are available now at the Information Desk in the University Center. 
Completed petitions are due by 5 p.m. Wednesday, April 23. Senator candi
dates need 25 signatures, names and email addresses of constituents. Presi
dent and Treasurer candidates need 100 signatures.
&becTATvbcdB When you run for office or come out to cast a ballot, 
you help shape the future of the campus. Get involved in student govern
ment  were working for you.
Elections are being held again due to procedural errors.

 1 11 11 \1 i * l
movies you may have seen before....
By GREG MARCKS
Thursday, April 24
Film Fest Six
For the last five years, filmmaking@cmuhas spon
sored a student film festival where one can kick 
back, munch on some Rice Krispie Treats, and 
watch some bad-ass independent films and videos. 
Last year, audiences swooned during the screening 
of a little film called Elevator Gambling. (Ah, the 
glory of self-promotion.) This year, it is rumored 
that popular pom stars Diamond Lace and Ed The 
Elephant McVicker may make an appearance. 
And who knows? One of your fellow classmates may 
become a famous filmmaker someday, and youll be 
able to say, I knew her when she sucked, or That 
guy used to write on his tongue with a Sharpie.
At 7r30, 10 pm, and 12:30am
In McConomy
Friday, April 25
The English Patient
Speaking of sucking, this does. But dont worry, 
Im the only person who feels that way. My favorite 
part of the whole movie is when Kristin Scott 
Thomas tries to leave Ralph Fiennes and then she 
whacks her head on a pole. Lets see that one again 
in super slo-mo! CLONG! Ooh, now thats drama.
And while Im ranting needlessly, has anyone 
noticed that Willem Dafoe is crappy? I mean, he 
seems like the kind of guy who offers to check your 
tire pressure just so he can steal your hubcaps and 
sell them for shampoo.
Incidentally, this movie is long and beautifully 
photographed and based on a novel by Michael 
Ondaatje. I think it won an award or something.
At 7 and 10 pm
In McConomy
Saturday, April 26
Jerry Maguire
Well, I can see weve got our plates full this week. 
OK, so everyone thought this was Tom Cruises best 
performance ever, or at least thats what the com
mercials tried to make us believe. Hes a sleazeball 
sports agent who gets fired and takes on some wide 
receiver who makes him perform childish stunts 
over the phone like Bark like a dog! and Beat 
yourself senseless with your own torso! just for his 
own perverted kicks.
Cameron Crowe directed this flick with numerous 
celebrity cameos. It was photographed by Janusz 
Kaminski, best known for his work on Cool As Ice.
If you say, Show me the money, you lose a 
testicle.
At 7:30, 10 pm, and 12:30 am
In McConomy
Sunday, April 27
The Devils
Get this. This 1971 British celluloid strip stars 
Vanessa Redgrave and is based on an Aldous Huxley 
novel of the same name. The story takes place in 
pre-Renaissance France, where some big-shot Car
dinal is trying to take over the whole jurisdiction. 
But this one priest, he wont give up his abbey, see? 
So the Cardinal, he transforms the guy into this 
warlock in charge of a devil-possessed nunnery 
where the Mother Superior is sexually obsessed 
with him. Pretty neat punishment, huh? Im not 
sure exactly how he thought making him more 
powerful would defeat him but anyway this mad 
witch-hunter comes to town and theres a big trial so 
its a courtroom drama.
At 8, 10 pm, and midnight
In McConomy
Name the Quote:
Did you try staples?
(It fit so nice, he said I could keep it.Andr the 
Giant in The Princess Bride)
